## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object in chemical kinetics rate-law modeling. With only t and A available, the most plausible relationships are autonomous or time-varying kinetic ODEs (e.g., nth-order decay, reversible relaxation toward equilibrium, autocatalysis, or time-dependent effective rate constants).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when reactant is abundant or surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order (self-reaction) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption with only A observed)
- General nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical order or lumped kinetics)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (nonlinear): dA_dt = c0 * (c1**c2 - A**c2) (nonlinear driving force / generalized mass-action toward equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type production-consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplification with carrying capacity/limiting depletion)
- Quadratic autocatalysis with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * (c1 - A) (stronger autocatalysis or chain-branching with depletion)
- Parallel decay channels (linear + nonlinear): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (multiple pathways lumped into effective terms)
- Time-dependent first-order rate (exponential drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * A (temperature/catalyst activity drifting in time, lumped into k(t))
- Time-dependent first-order rate (power-law drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t**c2) * A (aging/conditioning effects producing k(t) trends)
- Forcing/feeding term + first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 + (-c1 * A) (continuous production/inflow with linear consumption)
- Periodic modulation of rate constant: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic temperature/illumination modulation in kinetic experiments)
- Empirical rational inhibition (self-inhibition with only A observed): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate slows at high A due to inhibition/transport limits)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If A decays exponentially with constant half-life, dA_dt is typically proportional to -A (first-order).
- If 1/A vs t is approximately linear, dA_dt often contains a -A**2 term (second-order self-reaction).
- A linear approach to a nonzero plateau suggests a driving-force form c*(A_eq - A), indicating reversible kinetics or replenishment toward equilibrium.
- An inflection in A(t) with initial acceleration then slowing (sigmoidal A(t)) is consistent with autocatalysis terms like A*(A_max - A).
- If the apparent decay rate changes systematically with time, model it as a time-dependent effective rate constant k(t) multiplying A (e.g., k(t)=c0+c1*exp(c2*t) or k(t)=c0+c1*t**c2).
- If A(t) shows oscillatory deviations around a trend, introduce periodic modulation in the rate coefficient via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) factors on A.
- If the rate magnitude grows faster than linearly with A at high concentration, include higher powers A**c (chain reactions/branching/lumped nonlinearities).
- If the rate magnitude saturates at high A (transport/inhibition-limited), use rational forms like A/(c + A) multiplying a maximum rate scale.

Key structural facts: (i) purely algebraic rational function in \(A\) (no trig/log/exp), (ii) only even powers; (iii) denominator is quartic-in-\(A\) plus constant, specifically \(1+0.7498A^4\); (iv) overall behavior \(\sim -0.18998A^2\) for large \(A\).

I’ll check whether each candidate can be parameter-set to exactly this function on a plausible domain (typically \(A\ge 0\)).

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK0)

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidates evaluated: 82
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

**GT numerical expression:**
$$f(A) = -0.18998 \cdot A^2 + \frac{0.45987 \cdot A^2}{0.74980 \cdot A^4 + 1}$$

This is a rational function with two terms: a polynomial term $-c_0 A^2$ and a rational term $\frac{c_2' A^2}{c_4 A^4 + 1}$.

Let me combine over a common denominator:
$$f(A) = \frac{-0.18998 \cdot A^2(0.74980 A^4 + 1) + 0.45987 A^2}{0.74980 A^4 + 1}$$
$$= \frac{-0.14244 A^6 - 0.18998 A^2 + 0.45987 A^2}{0.74980 A^4 + 1}$$
$$= \frac{-0.14244 A^6 + 0.26989 A^2}{0.74980 A^4 + 1}$$

So the GT is a rational function of the form:
$$f(A) = \frac{\alpha A^6 + \beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1}$$

with $\alpha < 0$, $\beta > 0$.

Now I need to check which candidates can match this. The key structural features:
- It's a function of A only (not t)
- It's a rational function with numerator having $A^6$ and $A^2$ terms, denominator having $A^4$ and constant terms
- No transcendental functions (sin, cos, log, exp)

Let me quickly categorize candidates:

**Candidates with sin/cos/log/exp that can't be zeroed out:** Many candidates contain sin(...) or log(...) or exp(...) terms. If these transcendental terms can be set to zero by choosing constants, the candidate might still match. Let me check if the sin terms can be zeroed (set amplitude coefficients to 0) and if the remaining rational structure matches.

**Candidates with rational structure over $(A^5 + c_1)$:** Many candidates have denominator $A^5 + c_1$. The GT has denominator $\gamma A^4 + 1$. These are fundamentally different - $A^5$ vs $A^4$ in the denominator. These CANNOT match unless the $A^5$ terms cancel.

Let me check candidates with $A^{3/2}$ denominators: These have denominator $A^{3/2}c_1 + \sqrt{A}c_2 = \sqrt{A}(Ac_1 + c_2)$. The combined fraction would be:
$$\frac{\text{numerator}}{\sqrt{A}(Ac_1 + c_2)}$$

The GT denominator is $\gamma A^4 + 1$, which is fundamentally different.

Let me focus on candidates that could potentially produce the right structure.

**Candidate 10 (and similar sqrt-based candidates):**
Common denominator: $A^{3/2}c_1 + \sqrt{A}c_2 = \sqrt{A}(Ac_1 + c_2)$

The numerator terms include $A^{5/2}, A^{3/2}, \sqrt{A}, A, c_9$. After dividing by $\sqrt{A}(Ac_1+c_2)$, we get terms like $A^2/(Ac_1+c_2)$, $A/(Ac_1+c_2)$, etc. But one term is $A^{3/2}c_3/(A^{3/2}c_1 + c_2)$ which has a DIFFERENT denominator. This breaks the structure.

For the pure rational candidates with denominator $A^{3/2}c_1 + \sqrt{A}c_2$, if ALL terms share this denominator, the combined expression is a polynomial in $\sqrt{A}$ divided by a linear function in $A$. This cannot produce $A^4$ in the denominator.

**Candidates with $A^5 + c_1$ denominator and sin terms that can be zeroed:**

Looking at candidates like **Candidate 57**: Setting $c_3 = 0$ and $c_8 = 0$ (zeroing sin terms):
$$\frac{c_0 A^6 + c_2 A^5 + c_7 A}{A^5 + c_1}$$

This gives $\frac{c_0 A^6 + c_2 A^5 + c_7 A}{A^5 + c_1}$, but GT needs $\frac{\alpha A^6 + \beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1}$. These have different denominator degrees (5 vs 4). **Cannot match.**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the GT's rational structure with $A^4$ denominator.

Let me verify: every candidate either has transcendental functions that can't fully replicate the rational structure, or has wrong polynomial/rational degree structure.
